<Text>Jenna Aguon was guest tatooing at Avalon II, and she did my tattoo. She is so sweet, wonderful, talented, and has a gentle hand with the tattoo machine. She did a great job of making time fly by with our conversation,  and she genuinely cared about what I had to say. Most importantly, my tattoo came out infinitely better than I could have ever imagined.

Solid Chinese spot. We tried the general tsao chicken, may Lee veggies and pepper beef and they were all solid. Nice flavor, great portion size, very legit American Chinese food. <name>Chris Conner< /name><Time>1279428387571< /Time><Rate>3</Rate><text>it isnt exactly the BEST chinese food that i have ever had, but it is far from the worst. as many have said before me, it seems as if this buisness thrives on deliveries... but i ordered take out, so i can not comment on the delivery times.

i stopped by on my way home to pick up a quick lunch special. i ordered the spicy salt and peper pork rib and forked down the extra 80 cents to upgrade to chow mein. the pork rib was battered and deep fried... which was unexpected, and it turned out to be a touch oily. despite this minor flaw, it was perfectly seasoned, hot and delicious. the chow mein was veggie chow mein and the noodles were thicker than i am used to, but was far from the cheap generic stuff that you can find on every corner.

i have walked passed the place a few times before the smells finally enticed me to come inside. my first impression of the food wasnt bad... but wasnt great, but it was good enough to get me to go back and check out some of their a la carte items. the dinning room is really small, only 3 or 4 tables MAX.

i would recommend take out or delivery. the place isnt really flashy either, so it might be a turn down to some people in that nature.

i would suggest to at least try it for yourself... it is worth that much at least</text><pics>None</pics><resp>None<//resp>< Gmap_id>

However, placing orders from them is almost a nightmare.
1) Their website is not very intuitive, and when you get to the point of checkout if you use an unsupported card (like Amex), it just says your card is decliend.  Not that your card isn't a valid type for this business.
2) When the website was difficult to use, we opted to call our order in.  This place doesn't seem like they ever want to answer their phone.  We spent 5+ minutes trying over and over before we finally got someone on the phone.
3) Ordering a drink from the bar is a nightmare when the bartender doesn't acknowledge you were there when he was off chatting it up with other guests, then just left to go back into the kitchen. Went here for breakfast on a Saturday morning. They open at 9:00am, but the kitchen is not ready until 9:30. Otherwise, the breakfasts are huge portions and taste like everything is made from scratch, whether that's actually true I don't know. The bloody Mary's are just $5.00 and they come in a pint glass with olive, celery, and bacon strip, and are moderately spicy, but you can ask for it mild. The service seems slow, perhaps short-handed, or maybe just slow in the morning. Food preparation seemed slow too, but worth the wait.</review>

< Review>
I moved here from New York, couldn‚Äôt find a decent slice of pizza, tried a few random spots, then I found north beach pizza because someone praised it on Twitter or Reddit, and I was thoroughly impressed. I usually get a small cheese pizza and a small salad with Italian dressing. The pizza is really good, it‚Äôs doughy, the sauce is really good, just the right amount of cheese. My favorite part of a pizza is the sauce-y river where the cheese meets the crust. I usually pick my first slice based in which one is the biggest or which slice is the best looking. The salad is really good too, I don‚Äôt eat enough vegetables but I like their salads, the vegetables are fresh. I get the Italian dressing, I try to commit to finishing the salad before I go for the pizza but I don‚Äôt always make it. I started ordering larger pizzas, wrapping up the extra slices for lunch the next day or two. Oh! the pizza comes with a little thing of Parmesan and red pepper flakes, that is a nice touch. The salad comes with a fork and some great durable napkins, it you know how to fold them properly you can really make them last. So yea overall I think they got the best pizza in town, at least compared to the few random spots I tried.< /Review>

< review>
Good news is that the food was really tasty. But... Overpriced and coupled with poor service today. There are too many other options to give this place another chance.
Specific issues include:
I understand (kinda) the use of qr code menus. But it's annoying. Just give me a paper copy.
Put your prices on your menu!!! I get that places don't always provide their menu prices online. Then make another option so I can see what I'm paying when I'm your establishment...
The entrees are overpriced. The (tasty) buffalo chicken sandwich was $13. With no side. The side of fries (a true side order, not a basket) was $4. It's just not worth 17$ for sando w fries. Even the plainest of burgers was $9. Maybe I just don't understand?
I asked for ranch!! It wasn't busy. Or how about I don't have to wait (literally) 20 minutes after eating to get my bill?< /review>

<text>The atmosphere here is great. There is one entire wall of open aired windows and a large, u-shaped bar. Unfortunately, we've had very spotty service and inconsistent food.
This place specializes in the ability to modify any dish however you want. However, whenever we've asked for mods, the kitchen has ignored it and we've had to send the dish back. Very frustrating.
Don't sit at the bar if you expect attentive service. The bartenders are always swamped and under-staffed. They are friendly though.
There are a few breakfast dishes that stand out--both the Chilaquiles Benedict and the Smoked Salmon Benedict are delicious.
This place would be a good spot to grab drinks and socialize with friends.</text>< pictures>

I certainly understand your perspective and appreciate the opportunity to explain.  Because of our totally customizable menu, we have an ingredient-centric pricing structure.  So, as guests remove ingredients from their meal, the price goes down (which is a unique aspect to STACKED) and when guests add ingredients the price goes up.  Over 95% of our guests either start from scratch to build their meal, or modify an existing signature item.  So, if we had prices on the paper menu, hardly any guest would actually be paying the listed price.  We felt this would cause a great deal of frustration and confusion for our guests. That's why we only have prices on the digital menu, where you can see the price change as modifications are made.  I hope this explanation helps.  Thanks again for visiting STACKED!"}<//resp>< gmap_id>

< text>
An interesting concept where you use an iPad to build your own burgers, salads, etc. For every item you add/remove you can see the cost increase/decrease. The service was friendly and the decor was nice.

In practice it took too long for our party to place an order because not every possible option was programmed into the software and we had to get help with a couple items. The food itself was fine but the ordering experience was a bit frustrating and makes me not want to return.

There is an option for the waiter to take your order but you have no idea how much everything costs because the physical menus have no prices.<//text>

Though a bit on the pricey side, great place for a good burger.
Stacked recently opened in my area and from the 3 times I've been there I have seen that it consistently gives a good burger among other food items. Their mac and cheese is not too bad either though it can get a bit on the greasy side.

I understand your concern about prices on the printed menu and I appreciate the opportunity to respond.  We have an ingredient-centric menu, including pricing.  Every ingredient has a value associated with it, so if you remove an ingredient from a signature item, the price goes down (which is unique to STACKED), and if you add an ingredient the price goes up.  Over 95% of our guests modify their meals in some way, so the price they pay is very rarely the price that would be displayed on a paper menu.  We feel that this would cause a lot of confusion for our guests.  The prices are clearly marked on the iPad menu, and guests can see them change as they add or subtract ingredients. <username>Patrick Vogel<//username><Date>1547874229565< /Date><rating>1</rating><Review>My wife and I were excited to try a new restaurant....We are in the area a lot for the local retail, Dick's Sporting Goods, Nordstrom Rack and many others in the immediate area....We have watched the building of the store along with the throngs of people going in and out for the last several months....
Okay, getting to the point....You can have great food...(or in our case mediocre food)....A cool vibe, and decor....Attractive servers and staff.....But having it all is the trick that restaurants have been trying to perfect for many years....Look, there is a reason why In-N-Out only makes essentially three things....
But Stacked is no In-N-Out....and in this spirit that they can not focus on any one area....Super Sad...but this can happen to any new restaurant....
Now going back to our experience, we sat at the bar...We had three young ladies one prettier than the next serving us....But none of them had a clue how to serve or the organizational fortitude to see what was requied and how to insert their services when required....Look, we asked to see a menu....After a few minutes we received menues....We ordered drinks, but waited longer than what is normally required....Remember, we were sitting at the bar....not in some distant obscure both forgotten about...Why ask customers how they want there burger cooked if your not going to cook it in our case medium rare....The burger was cooked well done....This begs the question, why open another restaurant that spends more on decore than training....I get it, a cool looking restaurant always looks good on paper....These are the restaurants that fail....The ones that look good on paper....We all have favorite restaurants that we grew up....None of these restaurants had business plans or lofty goals to take over the food industry....No they had a different plan all together, make a great meal for a stranger and hope they come back....Well Stacked never got that message...And unfortunately did not stack up to this patrons expectations....Remember we all have choices....Do not settle for anything but the best.......<//Review><Pics>None</Pics>< Resp>

< review>
We love stacked.  Normally it is always a five star.  Last night we received a fried egg that was well done on our burger.  This was the second time in a week that this has happened in the last week at the Huntington Beach store.  After eating a meal size salad we had to ask for our burger because it hadn't been brought back.  A bit of training needs to happen for the staff on Wednesday nights.  Other than the two egg incidences we have never had a problem at Stacked.  We love their food.  Both my husband and I are gluten free and grain free.  Hubs is also milk free.  Most of the menu at stacked accommodates our dietary restrictions.

I had lunch at the stacked in Cerritos with a friend 3 days ago.  The food was just as good as our normal H.B. store.  The atmosphere was not as fun as Huntington Beach.  The Cerritos store was a bit dark and the music wasn't as lively compared to Huntington.  The wait staff was excellent.  As I said above we love eating at Stacked.  We are in California 4-5 months a year and Stacked is our go to restaurant over all others.< /review>

<time>1497462788792< /time><rating>4<//rating><Text>I was really excited to try this place once I found out about its concept. What blew me away even more what the ambiance and indoor/outdoor theme they really blended well. For HB - this was a totally cool way to capture hanging out with friends, with an ice cold beer and a burger.

We popped in for lunch on Friday. We sat on the high tops near the patio and enjoyed the nice breeze. The concept is you order your food/drinks from the iPad and it gets delivered to your table as soon as it's ready. When your ready to pay, you can simply swipe your credit card on the ipad device and you're outta there in a hot min!

The food was amazing. Build your own burgers, or try a fun spin on their popular ready made menu items. Great food, great beers, great service.

You've got us hooked!!< /Text><pics>None</pics>< Resp>

<review>Chocolate Chunk Brownie ($8.70 as stacked) is topped with double fudge brownie ice cream, toasted coconut, Reese‚Äôs Peanut Butter Cups, peanut butter sauce, and whipped cream. This is a rich and heavy dessert, yet decadent. The brownie itself is not too dense and hot and gooey right out of the oven. The peanut butter flavor from the sauce and Reese‚Äôs pairs nicely with the uber chocolate flavors. Peanut butter plus chocolate equals onolicious! This is definitely a dessert for the chocoholic in your life, like my hubby! Rating: 5/5

Butter Cake ($10.55 as stacked) is topped with strawberry ice cream, blackberries, blueberries, strawberries, raspberries, almonds, and whipped cream. The butter cake reminds me of pound cake in texture and holds up to any topping you pile on it. It has a neutral taste so you can go to any ‚Äúflavortown‚Äù you please from fruit to chocolate. I personally loved it with the berries. Their natural sweetness and tanginess bring out the vanilla in the cake. As the strawberry ice cream starts to melt, it turns into a sauce that lends more moisture to the cake. I would really love to see this option on the permanent menu!!! Rating: 5/5

Pumpkin Bread Pudding ($7.75 as stacked) is topped with banana, strawberries, strawberry sauce, chocolate sauce, caramel sauce, almonds, and whipped cream. If you are a pumpkin lover like I am, you‚Äôll love this bread pudding. It has a nice pumpkin pie flavor from the nutmeg and cinnamon. I went a little overboard on the toppings and would keep it more minimal next time with more neutral flavors; maybe with just the caramel sauce, almonds, and whipped cream. Rating: 4.5/5< /review></record>

<username>Shaunna Hargrave< /username>< Date>

<Rate>3< /Rate><Review>Good food but not good enough for the price, in my opinion.

PRICING: Everything is priced a la carte and you build ("stack") your order, with each component being an additional charge. To get something really gourmet and special, you'll easily be looking at $11.50 for the burger *alone*, no sides.

PORTIONS: The burger was at least a decent size. The side of fries was small. My simple 4 ingredient salad was smaller than anything I've ever had at a restaurant. The meat portion was good, but the salad was even smaller than what many restaurants call a "petite" version.

FOOD TASTE & QUALITY:  Don't get me wrong, the burger was delicious. Juicy and flavorful. The garlic parmesan fries were tasty, but quite oily at the bottom. The steak salad was... MEH.

SERVICE:  You can have them give you standard table service, but it really is better geared to place your order on the table-side iPads. "Stacking" your order is easier if you do it, than trying to have the wait staff hear you in the very loud environment. It's kind of cool. They were pretty efficient with everything, but it does seem to leave an element of confusion to the service. Everyone helps all tables, it seems, so the lack of delegation meant sometimes I was passed without drinks refilled, but random staff did pop in to check on us. The chaos is distracting. I'd rather have staff you know I'm their responsibility, rather than have every other worker interrupt my lunch to see if I'm taken care of.

Bottom line, I just can't see paying these prices for this service and quality.< /Review><Pics>None< /Pics>< Response>
None</Response>
